## Analysis

$$0.4867 \cdot P^{1/3} + 0.4867 \cdot P \cdot \exp(-0.08577 \cdot t)$$

This has two terms: a $P^{1/3}$ term and a $P \cdot \exp(-ct)$ term.

**Candidate 15**: `P**(1/3)*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + c3*t*exp(c4*t) + c5*exp(c6*t)`

This can be written as:
$$c_0 \cdot P^{1/3} + c_1 \cdot P \cdot \exp(c_2 \cdot t) + c_3 \cdot t \cdot \exp(c_4 \cdot t) + c_5 \cdot \exp(c_6 \cdot t)$$

Setting:
- $c_0 = 0.4867$ (matches the $P^{1/3}$ coefficient)
- $c_1 = 0.4867$ (matches the $P \cdot \exp$ coefficient)
- $c_2 = -0.08577$ (matches the exponential decay rate)
- $c_3 = 0$ (eliminates the $t \cdot \exp(c_4 t)$ term)
- $c_5 = 0$ (eliminates the $\exp(c_6 t)$ term)
- $c_4, c_6$ can be any values (their terms vanish)

This gives exactly:
$$0.4867 \cdot P^{1/3} + 0.4867 \cdot P \cdot \exp(-0.08577 \cdot t)$$

which matches the GT perfectly.
